Yuan Shaochang Departed for Hankou Last Night to Take Up His New Post 123

▲ Colleagues from the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway See Him Off at the Riverfront

Yuan Shaochang, the former Deputy Chief of Traffic of the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway, has served the railway for nineteen years. He started as a trainee station master and was promoted to the position of Chief under the favor of his superiors. During his tenure, he maintained harmony between superiors and subordinates. Although he was under the economic aggression of British imperialism, he was neither arrogant nor humble in his dealings with foreigners on official matters. He was especially meticulous in protecting his Chinese subordinates. Minister Sun of the Ministry of Railways is currently reorganizing the Pinghan Railway and urgently needs talent. Mr. Yuan's performance throughout his career has been excellent, so he was promoted to Chief of Traffic of the Pinghan Railway to assist in the reorganization. When his colleagues at the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway first heard the Ministry's order, they planned to jointly telegraph the Ministry to retract the order. However, because Mr. Yuan was being promoted, it was inappropriate to forcibly retain him. All colleagues felt reluctant to part with him. Mr. Yuan departed for his new post in Hankou on the Taikoo Company's Wusong ship last night. More than a hundred staff members of the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway went to the port to see him off, and even station workers went in groups to send him off, demonstrating Mr. Yuan's popularity among railway workers.

The Female Guest Turned Out to Be a Thief 124

▲ An Amusing Incident During the Wedding Feast

A Ningbo man surnamed Zhou, who resides at the southern end of Dongchang Road in Pudong, was celebrating his son's wedding the other day. As a result, his relatives and friends were seated to capacity. Unexpectedly, a well-dressed young woman was also drinking at the table. The young woman then took the little girl of Yao Xu, who was sitting next to her, to play with. Ms. Xu did not suspect anything because she thought the woman was also a wedding guest. Unexpectedly, the young woman cut off a gold lock pendant that the little girl was wearing with scissors. After the deed, she returned the little girl. At that time, the girl's parents had not yet noticed. Soon after, the young woman removed a small gold ring from the hand of Mr. Chen's son, another guest. However, the operation was not done discreetly and was spotted by another female guest surnamed Shen. She immediately grabbed the young woman and questioned her background, but her answers were all false. The other female guests at the table were enraged and slapped her in the face. The young woman's face turned red, and she knelt on the ground begging for mercy. She was then taken to the Third District Public Safety Bureau. After inspecting the young woman, the district chief found that she was dressed luxuriously and wore two sets of gold jewelry inside and out. He could not believe that she would resort to such low means. He interrogated her, and she confessed that her name was Chen Wang, she was thirty-two years old, and she lived in Zhangjiatang, Yu Family Temple, Pudong. She worked in the British-American Tobacco Company's Third Factory. The rest of her words were evasive. The district chief ordered her to be detained for further investigation.

Young Woman Takes Her Own Life Out of Pride 125

▲ Scolded by Her Foster Mother for Disobedience

▲ Took Poison Out of Anger

A woman named Shen Zheng, who resides at No. 66 half door plate of Fujian Road, makes a living by washing clothes. The other day, she went out after hanging up the washed clothes to dry. Unexpectedly, it suddenly rained. Upon returning home, she saw that the clothes were all soaked. She scolded her foster daughter Yang Wenkui, saying that she should not have stood idly by. The girl, who was already eighteen years old, was very proud. She was scolded and became disobedient. Out of anger, she swallowed opium paste. By the time Ms. Shen realized it, she had already been deeply poisoned. Although she was sent to the hospital, there was no way to save her. She died the other day. Upon receiving the report, the Old Gate Police Station sent detectives to transport the body to the burial parlor on Fielun Road. They also invited Prosecutor Guo from the Special District Court to come to the parlor to examine the body and inquire about the reason for the girl's suicide. They then instructed Shen Zheng to sign a bond to claim the body for burial.

Difficulties for Prostitutes to Turn Over a New Leaf 126

▲ Living Together Privately with a Patron

▲ Lured Back by the Brothel Owner and Others

Zhu Changlin from Liyang died of illness in his hometown the year before last. Because his wife had difficulty making a living due to poverty, she brought her daughter Caiying to Shanghai. At that time, the girl was just of age. Although she was a village girl, she was quite beautiful. Zhu's wife pawned her to the Zhihua brothel at No. 505 Fuxiang Lane, Hankou Road, for three years, receiving a pawn fee of sixty yuan per year. The brothel owner Weng Ding initially ordered her to lure lustful men at various entertainment venues. The girl was only able to lure people in that way. In December of last year, she met a young man from Hangzhou named Zhong Hongbi, who opened the Datong Bicycle Shop at No. 248 Wuding Road. Zhu learned that Zhong was still unmarried and quite sincere, so she decided to turn over a new leaf. She asked Zhong to pull her out of the mire. Zhong agreed. The girl was eager to leave the brothel as soon as possible, so she did not wait for the brothel owner's permission and followed Hongfu's elopement. Since the girl disappeared, the brothel owner sent out detectives to search for her. It was not until the other day that she learned that she was living together with Zhong. She immediately gathered her nephew Weng Heshang, Chen Ganqing, Yan Hesheng, Xi Yunzhou, and others, and went to Wuding Road, and by using trickery managed to lured the Zhu girl out. They hired a rickshaw and planned to bring her back to the brothel. Midway, the girl screamed loudly. Officer Wang Youshan of the Gordon Road Police Station happened to pass by and inquired about the situation. They were all taken to the police station the other day and transferred to the Special District Local Court. Judge Sun Yuan questioned Zhu Caiying about her experience of turning over a new leaf and requested the judge to fulfill her wish so that she and Zhong could become a couple. Zhong also came to the court and stated that he was willing to grow old together. The defendants hired lawyer Fan Gang and requested bail. Judge Sun instructed the defendants to each pay 500 yuan in bail and adjourned the hearing for seven days.

Two Apprentices' Joking Leads to One Death 127

▲ Cai Qianxiang Dies from Serious Injuries

Cai Qiansan, a Yin family resident, has a son named Qianxiang, who is sixteen years old. He is an apprentice at the Dalong Machinery Factory in Tanziwan, Zhabei. The other afternoon, he was joking with his companion Wang Baogen, and his head was hit by an iron bar. He was taken to Baolong Hospital for treatment. He died from his injuries at 8:00 AM yesterday.

Each Has Their Own Reasons for Attempting Suicide by Poisoning 128

▲ Two Women and One Man: Two Dead, One in Critical Condition

▲ A Couple Quarreled: Shen Mingzhao, a 41-year-old Ningbo native, lives at No. 200 Shanqing Lane, Aierjin Road. He runs the Shen Mingji Tobacco Leaf Shop. His wife, Guo, is 27 years old. She likes to play mahjong all day and all night, neglecting her housework. Yesterday, Shen scolded her slightly. She harbored resentment and secretly swallowed raw tobacco in an attempt to commit suicide. She was discovered and taken to Tongren Hospital, then transferred to Guangren Hospital for treatment. Because too much time had passed, her life is in danger.

▲ Difficulties in Livelihood: Chen Zhongxian, a 28-year-old local resident, lives at No. 427 Fangbang Bridge, West Gate. Because he has been unemployed for several years and has difficulty making a living, he suddenly had suicidal thoughts. Yesterday, he secretly swallowed opium paste. This morning, his grandfather discovered him and ordered someone to take him to Renji Hospital for treatment. Because the poison had already attacked his heart, he died at around 3:00 PM.

▲ Angered by Her Husband's Scolding: Dong Agen, a 25-year-old Cantonese native, lives at No. 98 Tongchun Lane, Gongping Road. He used to be a chief steward on a ship sailing from Shanghai to Shantou. His wife, Li, is 19 years old and loves gambling. She lost repeatedly, causing all her jewelry to be pawned. Unexpectedly, Dong's ship happened to sail to Shanghai the other day. Someone informed Agen of the situation. After arriving home, he quarreled with her and returned to the ship to spend the night. The ship then sailed to Shantou the next afternoon. After being humiliated by her husband that night, she went to bed and did not get up. After being persuaded by her neighbors, she was peaceful overnight. Yesterday (the 20th) at around 3:00 PM, she had not yet gotten up. Someone entered the room to check on her and saw her moaning in bed, looking pale. They immediately hired a streetcar to take her to Tongren Hospital. However, because she had taken poison for too long, she died before reaching the hospital.

Seeking Death After Failing to Make a Living 129

▲ Tragic News of Zhou A'shan's Suicide by Slitting His Throat

Zhou A'shan, a lane sweeper in Dingxing Lane, North Sichuan Road, was 47 years old and from Ningbo. He lived at No. 27 in the lane and earned 15 yuan a month. He had a wife and two children, all of whom depended on Zhou's labor for a meager living. In Shanghai, where the cost of living is high, this was hardly enough to support a family of four, leading to increasing financial hardship and no possibility of borrowing. While they could barely manage in ordinary times, the price of rice rose sharply this year, and with a large appetite to feed, buying rice alone was difficult, let alone the seven necessities of life, all of which required money. Zhou A'shan was in such a state of desperation that he contemplated death. Yesterday morning, after getting up, Zhou, not wanting to neglect his duties, swept the lane clean. It was already eight o'clock. Upon returning home, he found their food supply exhausted and his pockets empty. Feeling despondent, he took out his own razor to trim his beard. Unexpectedly, before he could trim his beard, he turned the razor on his neck and slit his throat, severing his windpipe. He immediately fell to the ground and died.

His wife, Cao, tried to save him, but it was too late. She wailed and cried out in despair. Neighbors came to investigate and, upon understanding the situation, reported it to the police. The police in turn reported it to the First Precinct of the Fifth District, who ordered the local neighborhood head to report it to the local court for inspection. The prosecutor arrived at the scene and confirmed that it was a suicide. He instructed the family to arrange for the burial.

Father and Son Both Bandits 130

▲ Yangjiadu Robbery Case Solved

During the first month of the year, the Xi family, villagers in Wangjia Bamboo Garden, Yangjiadu, Pudong, were robbed by a gang who broke into their home armed with weapons and ransacked it. The victim, Mr. Xi, sounded the alarm, which resulted in him being shot in the foot by the robbers. The gang then fled in a commotion. Recently, the local Public Security Bureau arrested a suspect named Zhang Shaoyun. Zhang's son, Jinmao, was also implicated. The other day, together with Detective Liu Chunshu from the Old Gate Police Station, they apprehended Zhang Jinmao at the rooftop garden of the New New Company. He was then handed over to the Special District Court, where Judge Sun conducted a preliminary hearing and ordered him detained pending further investigation upon receiving official documents from the Public Security Bureau.

Case of Privately Trafficking Copper Coins 131

▲ Three Cases in One Day

Since the price of copper coins varies in different parts of the country, some people transport copper coins from one place to another, or even to a third place, profiting from the price differences. They consider this to be a lucrative business. However, customs officials are very strict in their searches, but these people are adept at concealing their contraband, making it difficult to detect. In the past two days, a total of three cases were uncovered: two involving smuggling out and one involving smuggling in. Details are recorded below:

▲ Smuggling Out (1) The day before yesterday, at 1:45 PM, near the outer barrier of the Suzhou steamer at the Huatong Wharf in Pudong, a boat approached and docked alongside the steamer. Two passengers on board had upper bodies that were noticeably bulging in both the front and back, a shape that was quite comical. A patrolling water police officer noticed this and, suspecting something amiss, approached and unbuttoned the passengers' coats. He found that they were covered in layers of copper coins, wrapped in canvas bags around their chests and backs, totaling 82,000 coins. The officer intended to take the two men to the water police station for processing, but one of them, named Li Xiaolizi, secretly offered the officer a silver dollar, attempting to bribe him to let them go. The officer refused and took the bribe money and the two men to the police station. Under interrogation, they confessed that one was Li Xiaolizi, 28 years old, from Jiangbei, and the other was Long Xiaolong, 27 years old, also from Jiangbei. They confessed that they intended to transport the copper coins to Hong Kong by steamer. The police chief, based on the confession, ordered the copper coins to be confiscated and handed over to customs. Long Xiaolong was released as it was his first offense, while Li Xiaolizi was charged with bribery and held for transfer to the local court for prosecution. (2) Yesterday morning around 7:00 AM, the Suzhou steamer of the Taikoo Company was loading cargo at the company's wharf on the Puxi side after crossing from the Huatong Wharf in Pudong. As the ship was scheduled to depart that day, customs officers boarded the ship to search for contraband as usual. They discovered five bags of copper coins, about 60,000-70,000, in the hold. The customs officers, as they had not finished their search, and the stevedores were busy loading cargo, making it difficult to search, ordered the stevedores to temporarily stop working. However, the stevedores refused, leading to a conflict. The Western head of the customs search team was punched in the back. The situation escalated, and the ship reported it to the water police station. Police officers boarded the ship to restore order, allowing the customs officers to continue their work.

▲ Smuggling In Song Haiyun, from Shangyu, was found carrying over 60,000 copper coins yesterday afternoon while passing near the Taikoo Company in Pudong. He was stopped by a patrol officer from the Third District, who took him and the copper coins to the district headquarters. Song confessed that he was 45 years old and worked as a tea server on the Taikoo New Ning steamer. He saw that the price of copper coins was rising in Shanghai, so he invested in buying these coins from Datong and planned to resell them for profit. The district chief ordered an investigation and further action.

Compensation for Damages in a Car Accident Case 132

Hu Yufang was previously hit by a car driven by Tian Yaoming, a driver for the Russian merchant company Laiyi. After receiving medical treatment, Hu felt that his losses were significant and hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit against Laiyi Company for compensation. The Special District Court held a hearing the other day, and the plaintiff invited a British soldier to testify. However, as the defendant failed to appear in court, the presiding judge adjourned the hearing to a later date. The defendant, Laiyi Company, has also hired lawyer Shen Yuesheng to write a defense statement, denying any responsibility for compensation.

Two Dancers in Paris Encounter Thieves 133

▲ Purse Snatch

▲ Recovered by Police

The other night, around 7:00 PM, two dancers from the Paris dance hall, one named Wang and the other named Feng, along with a "Miss Shi," were going to the Wing On Company to shop from their residence in Yuqing Lane, North Chengdu Road. While walking along Jing'an Temple Road, Wang's purse was suddenly snatched by a thief, Dong Jianglang, who fled. Fortunately, he was apprehended by police. Upon inspection, the purse contained 26 silver dollars, as well as other items, all of which were intact. The next morning, the police handed Dong over to the Special District Court for trial. Judge Wu, after questioning the thief, sentenced him to six months in prison, and the stolen items were returned to the original owner.

Prisoner Dies of Illness 134

Ding Baolong, from Jiangbei, 27 years old, was arrested in the French Concession for a crime and sentenced to imprisonment by the French court. He was sent to prison to serve his sentence. Currently, Ding became ill while in custody and was sent to Guangci Hospital for treatment by the prison warden. However, due to the severity of his illness, treatment was ineffective, and he died in the hospital on the afternoon of the 17th. The hospital notified the prison, which in turn notified the Tongren Fuyuan Hall to send someone to take the body to the morgue. The police station sent detectives to investigate and notify the family to claim the body for burial.

Fire in a Workshop in Huayuan Shiqiao, Pudong 135

Around 2:00 AM the other night, a fire suddenly broke out in a workshop owned by a Mr. Zhang in Huayuan Shiqiao, Pudong. The dense smoke spread quickly, threatening to engulf the area. The patrol police noticed and immediately sounded the alarm, waking the neighbors from their sleep. Together, they worked to extinguish the fire, which was brought under control and burned down a kitchen building. Afterward, the police took Liu Yunzhang, a worker at the workshop, and Jiang Shouqiao, the owner of a neighboring lumberyard, to the district headquarters. After questioning, it was determined that the fire originated in the workshop, and Liu was fined 10 yuan. Jiang Shouqiao was released as he was not involved.

Lay Buddhist Forest Invites Fan Gunong to Lecture on Sutras 136

The World Lay Buddhist Forest at the intersection of Xinmin Road and Guoqing Road in Zhabei is currently inviting lay Buddhist Fan Gunong to lecture on the Eight Great Awakenings Sutra every Saturday and Sunday afternoon. Those interested in studying Buddhism are welcome to attend.

Tax Exemption for Domestic Goods Advertising 137

The Shanghai Machinery Industry Association issued a notice yesterday (No. 266) stating: "Respectfully notifying that Shanghai Social Bureau Instruction No. 2211 was received, concerning the matter of exempting domestic goods advertising tax. It has now been resolved at the 153rd Municipal Council Meeting of this government that: A. Only rent will be charged for posting advertisements in public advertising spaces built by the Municipal Government; domestic goods advertising tax will be completely exempted. B. For goods advertised, original proof documents from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce or the former Municipal Agricultural and Commercial Bureau should be submitted to the Social Bureau for inspection to confirm that they are indeed domestic goods before the above method can be applied." Besides separately ordering the Bureau of Finance and the Bureau of Public Utilities, this is recorded for compliance. This order, etc., is hereby notified, and the association should comply with it. Please note."

Fine for Private Production of Red Pills 138

Zou Rongsheng, a detective from the French police, recently discovered that resident Xu An was privately producing and secretly selling red pills at his home, in violation of the prohibition. He went to Xu's residence and confiscated thousands of red pills, bringing them to the police station. The other day, he handed Xu over to the French court for investigation. The police chief first reported the circumstances, and Xu confessed to privately manufacturing and selling red pills. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Xu to a fine of 100 yuan, which was confiscated, and the confiscated red pills were destroyed.

Shen Bao Education News Special Issue of the Second National Education Conference No. 5

Fourth Day of the National Education Conference 141

Morning Participation in Scout Inspection

Afternoon Groups Continue Reviewing as Usual

Third General Assembly Held Today

Schedule Changed, Meeting Extended

The Second National Education Conference was on its fourth day yesterday. As members participated in the National Scout General Inspection yesterday morning, the General Assembly was suspended. However, various groups continued reviewing as usual in the afternoon. There were banquets at noon and in the evening. The details are recorded below:

All Members Participated in Scout Inspection Yesterday Morning 142

Members of the General Assembly departed from the Central Hotel at 8:30 AM to participate in the First National General Inspection of Chinese Scouts at the Xiaoying Parade Ground. The reception section of the General Assembly first distributed yellow guest badges sent by the Scout Headquarters to each member to wear. Upon arriving at the Xiaoying Parade Ground, the reception section prepared refreshments and rested in the reed shed in the guest seats. Zhang Yuqing and others from the reception section of the Scout Inspection Office cordially received them and asked the members to sign their names. Over forty people signed, including Zhu Jingnong, Chen Hexian, Chen Jianxiao, Xu Shouzhi, Wang Maozu, Sun Guiding, Wei Yu, Dai Chao, Huang Shiheng, Song Binggong, Liu Shimu, Liu Zhanen, Chen Heqin, Chen Bulei, Liao Shicheng, Li Quanshi, Zeng Guangming, Yang Zhongming, Jiang Ji, Liu Fazeng, and Sun Huiqing. Members such as Cai Yuanpei, Wu Zhihui, Li Shizeng, Jiang Menglin, and Shi Weihuan sat on the command platform and inspected all the scouts with Chairman Jiang. Chen Dezheng and Chen Bulei watched from the reporters' seats in front of the command platform. Most of the other members could only view from afar in the guest seats, and they regretted that they could not enter the parade ground to see the whole picture. Around 11:00 AM, they took cars back to the Central Hotel to rest.

Yesterday's Group Reviews 143

▲Higher Education Group's Third Review

Raising the Level of University and College Students

Establishing Career Paths for Graduates

Improving Qualifications for Sending Students Abroad

The Higher Education Group's third review meeting was held at the Ministry of Education yesterday, starting at 3:00 PM. Twenty-one people attended, including Huang Jianzhong, Shao Peizi, Sun Guiding, Dai Xiujun, Huang Shiheng, Xiong Mengfei, Dai Chao, Ou Yuanhuai, He Siyuan, Xie Shuying, Yang Xingfo, and Zhang Xindong. Yang Xingfo chaired the meeting, and Guo Youshou served as the recorder. The review covered: (1) Raising the level of students at universities and colleges and establishing career paths for graduates, deleting the last two sentences of Article 8; (2) Improving the method of sending students abroad. Huang Jianzhong first reported the various reasons and methods for provinces and cities to send students abroad during the period of political tutelage. This was followed by a discussion of the original proposal, completely deleting the second article and revising the third article as follows: Publicly funded students sent abroad should be limited to graduates from national, provincial, and registered universities or specialized education institutions, or research interns or service personnel from academic, industrial, or administrative organizations who have continued to work for more than one year and have passed examinations or reviews.

▲Overseas Chinese Group's Third Review

The entire proposal was passed after textual modifications to the original draft.

Requesting the Ministry of Education to Establish an Overseas Chinese Education Committee

The Overseas Chinese Education Group held its third review meeting on the 18th at 3:00 PM. Seven members attended, including Zhuang Zexuan, Liu Shimu, Qian Hezhong, Rong Guang, Ou Yuanhuai, Zheng Hongnian, and Zhu Baoqin. Zheng Hongnian chaired the meeting, and Zhu Baoqin served as the recorder. As a result, textual modifications were made to the entire original draft, deleting overly detailed clauses, and the entire proposal was passed. An additional clause was added, requesting the Ministry of Education to promptly establish an Overseas Chinese Education Design Committee as a legislative body for designing overseas Chinese education, to formulate detailed rules for the implementation of overseas Chinese education in the shortest possible time, and to hand them over to the Overseas Chinese Education Department for execution.

▲Mongolian and Tibetan Group's Second Review

General Agreement with the Original Proposal

Four Articles Modified in the Measures

The Mongolian and Tibetan Education Group held its second review meeting with committee members Wu Heling, Chen Xiaofan, Ku Qijun, Chen Yangfang, Wu Ruyi, Ma Hetian, and Wei Tingzheng attending. Ma chaired the meeting, and Ku served as the recorder. As a result of the review, there was general agreement with the original proposal, but detailed modifications were made to various measures as follows: (1) Measures for implementing educational administration: The Mongolian and League Departments shall be organized by their respective chiefs to form a League or Department Educational Administration Committee, subject to the supervision, guidance, and planning of the competent educational administrative yuan, and in charge of educational affairs within their respective League or Department; (2) Article 3 of the Measures for implementing general education: Each League and Department of Mongolia and important areas of Tibet shall establish a middle school, to be established uniformly within six years. The location and enrollment area shall be determined by the respective League or Department Educational Administration Committee, which shall formulate measures for establishing the school and submit them to the Ministry of Education for approval; (3) Article 1 of the Measures for implementing higher education: The recently promulgated regulations on the treatment of Mongolian and Tibetan students should be earnestly and fully implemented. Article 2 should follow the resolution of the State Council meeting in the spring of the 18th year, handed over to the Ministry of Education for handling, and establish a Mongolian and Tibetan class in the university before the start of the autumn semester this year; (4) Measures for compiling and printing educational books and magazines: Based on the Three Principles of the People and according to the Mongolian and Tibetan situation, compile and print textbooks for schools at all levels in Mongolian and Chinese, and Mongolian-Chinese bilingual, as well as popular reading materials with scientific or supplementary nature.

▲Social Education Group's Second Review

▲Establishing Key Public Institutions in Stages

The Social Education Group held its second review meeting, chaired by Lei Peihong, with Song Binggong as the recorder. Committee members present were Chen Hexian, Yu Qingtang, Wu Zhihui, Cai Yuanpei, Liu Mouen, Chen Jiansiu, Tang Maoru, Feng Bingkui, and Chen Zhengyi. As a result of the review: (1) The central government should establish key public institutions for social education within a limited time frame: 1. Public sports fields to be established within four years; 2. Public libraries to be established within eight years; 3. Public theaters to be established within twelve years; 4. Public museums to be established within sixteen years; 5. Public art galleries to be established within twenty years. Within these twenty years, related undertakings involving the above five institutions should be carried out in sequence; (2) Measures for planning special education and reformatory education: Adding that education for the mentally retarded and disabled should be piloted by the provincial education departments in conjunction with the civil affairs departments, etc., first in the provincial capitals and gradually推广 to all cities and counties; (3) New forms of entertainment to be promoted: A final note added that all kinds of entertainment equipment mentioned above must be replaced with domestic products as far as possible; (4) Measures for cooperation between social education and school education: Article 2 was deleted and replaced with schools at all levels should consider the situation and assist social education organizations and civic training groups to enable the public to use the four powers of the people. Rural normal schools and rural primary schools should pay particular attention.

Acting Director of Hebei Provincial Education Bureau, Sun Shiren

▲Teacher Training Group's Second Review

Establishing Qualifications for Entering Rural Normal Schools

Establishing Teacher Training Institutions

The entire proposal will be finalized today.

From 3:00 PM to 5:00 PM on the 18th, the Teacher Training Group held its second review meeting. Committee members Tao Xuan, Zhu Jingnong, Chen Dezheng, Meng Xiancheng, Xu Shoushang, Wei Que, Jin Zengcheng, Jin Baoshan, and Yu Ziyi attended, chaired by Tao and recorded by Jin. The review results were: (1) Establishing qualifications for entering rural normal schools: A. Graduates of senior elementary schools, aged 15 or above, to receive six years of normal education and training; B. Graduates of junior high schools to receive three years of normal training; C. Those who have served as rural primary school teachers and have the same level as junior high school graduates to receive three years of training. If there are special circumstances or special needs in various localities, those who have completed half of the original training time for normal students may be sent to serve in rural primary schools first and then supplement their training regularly until the original deadline; (2) Measures for establishing teacher training institutions: Article 1 originally stipulated that rural normal schools should be established in each county as a principle. Impoverished counties may jointly operate one school. The review opinion: Special cities may set up several rural normal schools according to actual needs. Article 2 was revised to say that normal schools and senior high school normal departments should be established by the province as a principle. All normal schools established by the provinces that have not been merged into senior high schools should continue to maintain their independence and strive to enrich their content. There is no need to urgently increase the number of schools. All provincial normal schools that have been merged into senior high schools may gradually separate them within a possible scope, depending on local conditions. If there is a special need for teachers, they may also submit a request to the Ministry of Education to entrust a relevant education institution to run the normal department on their behalf. Article 3 was revised to say that a rural normal college should be established in each province as a principle; (3) The curriculum review opinions of teacher training institutions at all levels are uniformly submitted to the drafting committee of the normal department curriculum standards, and this meeting will not discuss them; (4) Implementation Measures: Generally passed with amendments. Article 1 must analyze several aspects: the knowledge and skills required for teaching and training, and business aspects, and conduct systematic practice; (5) All three items of service treatment, vocational teacher training methods, and methods for advancing salaries for primary and secondary school teachers and staff will be reviewed this morning, and the entire proposal can be finalized. ▲Secondary Education Group's Third Review

The Secondary Education Group's third review meeting was chaired by Wang Maozu, with Wang Bingheng as the recorder. Liao Shicheng, Chen Bulei, Wu Jiaxiang, Zhao Naichuan, Lu Dianyang, Zhang Mojun, Lu Huangang, and Gu Shusen attended. The third section, subsection C of the second item of the Measures for Establishing Middle Schools, was revised again. The ratio of ordinary high schools to agricultural and industrial high schools should be based on the number of senior high schools in a province, with ordinary and agricultural and industrial departments each accounting for half. If the number of ordinary high schools and agricultural, industrial, and commercial high schools already established exceeds the ratio of three to one, the ordinary high schools that exceed the ratio should be converted into agricultural or industrial departments during the period of political tutelage before the review and approval. Add a new item E below: In provinces with only one high school, one more should be added during the period of political tutelage, so that each province has at least one ordinary high school and one agricultural or industrial high school when the period of political tutelage expires. The provincial education departments should formulate school establishment plans and submit them to the Ministry of Education for approval and implementation. The original item E was changed to item F and passed as the original. Section 5: Emphasis on initial learning experiments, passed as the original proposal. Section 6: Raising the level of ordinary high schools, the first item was revised: In addition to the establishment provisions in Section 3 of this plan, Section 2, provinces that establish ordinary high schools with simple equipment and poor performance should run junior high schools in provinces with better performance. Section 7: Revision of the implementation methods for vocational subjects, first, in addition to the planned internship for students in industrial high schools or vocational schools, the Ministry of Education will entrust experts to formulate separate methods for agricultural, commercial, and other internship methods, and the rest will be passed. Section 8: Reorganizing private middle schools, first, urging registration, A, the above article remains the same, and those who exceed the time limit should be ordered to suspend operations or order high schools to convert to junior high schools and junior high schools to convert to elementary schools. The first A was revised to those who have been running junior high schools or high schools for more than seven years, and the rest were passed. Chen Bulei and Wang Maozu were recommended to draft the Secondary School Moral Education Program. The first review meeting of the Elementary Education Group was chaired by Chen Heqin, Xu Xing, and Nie Tiren. As a result of the review: 1. Each province should consider the local situation and economic capacity to establish special schools for children, divided into three types: gifted, mentally retarded, and disabled schools. Each city and county should set up special children's classes. 2. Moral education and health education should be integrated into the curriculum as a whole.

▲Higher Education Group's Second Review Meeting

The Higher Education Group's second review meeting was attended by Cai Yuanpei, Yang Kofo, Shao Feizi, Ou Yuanhuai, Li Quanshi, Liu Zhanen, Dai Xiujun, Huang Shiheng, Guo Youshou, Huang Jianzhong, and other twenty people. The purpose should be to encourage the operation of private vocational schools and above, with special emphasis; (3) Regarding the sixteen articles on measures for universities and vocational schools to promote education, articles 2, 4, 6, 7, 6, 10, 11, 13, and 16 were cancelled, and item 12 was changed to establish various educational practical guidance centers.

If there are more ordinary middle schools and high schools already established, the agricultural and industrial departments should be converted separately during the period of political tutelage, depending on the circumstances; (3) According to the current survey, there are ten provinces that have not established high schools. Phonetic Literacy Case 146

▲Discussed at Today's General Assembly

▲The National Government Attaches Great Importance to It

The proposal to request the Ministry of Education to actively promote the phonetic literacy movement in the shortest possible time has the following reasons: Phonetic symbols are simple, easy to learn, less time-consuming, and more effective, which is the best way to assist literacy. Measures: 1. All people in the country, whether literate or illiterate, should uniformly use phonetic symbols; 2. Phonetic symbols are specially designed for the national pronunciation, but when necessary, local sounds may be added to facilitate promotion; 3. All popular reading materials should be marked with phonetic symbols; 4. All education institutions and popular education groups should organize a phonetic literacy design committee and appoint commissioners to be responsible for promotion. Proposers: Jing Heng, Dezheng, Gu Shusen, Liu Zhanen, Chen Heqin, Jingnong, Zengcheng, Ou Yuanhuai, Liu Fazeng, Li Quanshi, Hu Dinghua, Feng Liekui, Chen Rongjin, Huang Shiheng, Chen Zhengmo, Xiong Mengfei, Jiang Yi, Sun Shiren, Yu Qingtang, Yang Zhongming, Wang Jianzhong, Weng De, Lu Dianyang, Sun Huiqing, Yang Zhensheng, Zhao Naichuan, Li Zheng, Song Hugong, Zeng Guangming, He Siyuan, Cao Lei, Yuanpei, Yu Ying, Hexian, and Chen Jian. Lei Peihong and other twenty-six people. This case will be submitted to today's General Assembly for discussion, and it is heard that the Party and the National Government attach great importance to this case and have internally decided to submit it to the Central Political Conference for resolution next Tuesday and hand it over to the National Government for a nationwide announcement. Starting with Chairman Chiang, all personnel must learn phonetic alphabets.

Yesterday Afternoon's Grand Banquet at the Legislative Yuan 150

▲Solving Problems of Surname, Marriage, and Family

At noon on the 18th, Legislative Yuan Presidents Hu and Lin invited all members to the Yuan for a meal. More than a hundred members attended, including Cai Yuanpei, Li Shizeng, Wu Zhihui, Jiang Menglin, and Yang Xingfo. Hu Zhantang, Lin Zichao, Shao Yuanchong, and others accompanied them. During the meal, Hu Zhantang gave a speech, briefly stating that the colleagues of the Legislative Yuan welcome all members because the relationship between legislation and education is extremely close. The Legislative Yuan can only formulate the principles and guidelines from the Party's standpoint, and the detailed education plan must rely on the formulation of various experts. Therefore, the colleagues of the Legislative Yuan have great hope for all members and are very grateful for the hard work of all of you. I am a layman in education. I only studied at a crash course for normal schools in Japan for three months, which was thirty-three years ago. I returned to China to engage in education work and at the same time do revolutionary work, doing it twice, each time for only three and a half months, all of which failed due to revolutionary reasons. Since then, I can only sigh at the education work. The success of education and revolution is extremely important. Educators should have the spirit of revolution, and revolutionaries should also understand the principles of education. There is no difference between the two. Today, I have said a lot of nonsense, which cannot be used for your reference. I am afraid that you will not be able to digest some bad things you have eaten. Now, a comrade of the Legislative Yuan, standing on the legislative stage, has raised three questions, please ask the educators for advice, perhaps to help you digest, and I toast everyone a glass of water and wine, and wish you all good health. The three questions are raised for research:

The first question is the surname question (1) Do you want a surname? (2) Do you not want a surname? (3) If you want a surname, should it be the father's surname or the mother's surname?

The second question is the marriage question (1) Do you want to get married? (2) Do you not want to get married? (3) If you want to get married, is there a limit to early marriage or late marriage?

The third question is the family question (1) Do you want a family? (2) Do you not want a family? (3) If you want a family, is it better to have a big family or a small family?

Next, Chen Mengzhao, director of the Jiangsu Education Department, was publicly recommended by the members to give a reply, briefly saying that he was deeply grateful for the grand banquet hosted by the Legislative Yuan today. Mr. Hu is a master of education and a revolutionary master of education. From thirty-three years ago until now, he has never forgotten education and has always been working hard in education. He is our true revolutionary education mentor. I only represent my colleagues in requesting (1) Mr. Hu to come to the venue to give us a speech; (2) Leading revolutionary legal experts from the Legislative Yuan to guide our work. Today is the anniversary of the founding of the National Government. Please borrow a glass of wine from Mr. Hu and wish Mr. Hu good health, and shout long live the National Government. Afterwards, the discussion began. In order to save space, the answers of each member are recorded separately as follows:

The first question is the surname question (1) Zhong Rongguang: It is good to have a surname, and it is good not to have a surname. It is good to follow the father's surname, and it is good to follow the mother's surname. Hu Dinghua: Girls take the surname. If there are

girls in the university, they should take the surname. If there are no girls, they should not take the surname. (The reporter noted that Mr. Hu's school seems to have no girls, so it is not necessary to take the surname) Zhang Mojun: To maintain social order, there should be a surname. Children can freely choose their surname, but it should be limited to the parents' surname and cannot be a surname other than the parents'. Wu Zhihui: It is good to have it, and it is good not to have it. When someone invites me to eat, I must have a surname. When no one invites me to eat, I don't need a surname. Cai Jiemin: It is better not to have it. It is unfair to use the father's surname, and it is inappropriate to use the mother's surname. It is better not to have it. You can't use other symbols to replace it. Li Shizeng: The surname question is close to a natural science question. From the perspective of human genealogy in biology, in order to study human heredity and evolution, it seems necessary to preserve the surname. However, how to preserve the surname is another question. The naming method can be improved at any time. Jiang Menglin: This is a matter of time. Within fifty years, surnames are necessary.

The second question is the marriage question (1) Zhong Rongguang: Do not get married, especially people in the education field should not get married at all. If you are already married, do not have children (2) Hu Dinghua: Opposes not getting married, saying that if you do not get married, there will be no

young people in future generations, then the rice bowl problem of educators will be shaken (3) Zhang Mojun: Let people be free and see how each person's environment determines (4) Wu Zhihui: It is good to get married, because if someone gets married, someone will invite me, an old man, to be a witness, and I will get a great deal (5) Cai Jiemin: In the ideal new village, it is better not to get married. In this new village, there is a good organization, with single rooms for one person to stay and rooms for two people to sleep together. There are dance halls, entertainment rooms, and all kinds of equipment. When two people want to live in the same room, they must first be examined by a doctor and have a very accurate registration, such as when and what time someone lives in the same room. In the future, if children are born, there can be a mark. Li Shizeng merged the answer with the family question, because these two questions are close to social science questions and are very complicated and have great flexibility. From the perspective of the present teaching, he sympathizes with Mr. Cai very much. The marriage system and the family system both evolve with society. The future solution will definitely tend to shrink. Marriage shrinks to not getting married, and family shrinks to individual life. At the same time, there may need to be organizations with cooperative characteristics, just like what Mr. Cai said. In short, this is an evolving thing, and there can be no definite answer. In fact, it is gradually evolving towards a solution. For example, Mr. Tan Zhongda's marriage has abolished all wedding ceremonies, which is an example. Evolution is a common place for philosophy and science in the universe. Everything is evolving. All questions are summarized into scientific axioms. Morality is scientific and also an evolving thing. Solving these few questions cannot be an exception. Eight Jiang Menglin: Marriage is necessary within fifty years. Fifty years later, some people said that at that time, sexual diseases would be stopped, and not getting married would not be a problem. The third family question, one Zhong Rongguang is better not to have, two Wu Zhihui is better not to have, if you don't want it, you can specialize in eating other people's people, and you won't come to eat your own, three Cai Jiemin is better not to have it, if you have to, a small family is better than a big family, four Li Shizeng, (see the second question) five Jiang Menglin, it is necessary within fifty years, and whether you want a big family or a small family should depend on the economic and social development situation. In agricultural society, big families are needed, and in industrial society, big families are needed. After fifty years, it will be another question. After five hundred years, it will be even more incredible. At the end of the meeting, Mr. Hu Zhantang said that today I have listened to the high theory of all the gentlemen. Mr. Wu talked about facts, Mr. Jiang talked about theory, Mr. Li talked about science, and Mr. Jiang talked about time. They all have good answers to the questions we raised, which can be used for reference by the Legislative Yuan. I would like to thank you with a glass of wine. After the meeting, a photo was taken in the garden of the Legislative Yuan to commemorate the occasion.

Also, last night at 8:00 PM, the Examination Yuan held a banquet. Details will be published tomorrow.

Chairman Chiang's Banquet Last Night 151

▲Chung Yek-kwong's Response

At 5 PM, Chairman Chiang of the National Government, accompanied by his wife, Madam Soong Mei-ling, invited all members of the Lixingshe for a tea party. After being seated, Chairman Chiang called out each member's name and introduced them, then delivered an impromptu speech, saying that yesterday's speech still had shortcomings, and he hoped that everyone would contribute more ideas today. He emphasized that the most important aspect of education at present is popularization, something that everyone must have noticed. However, simply noticing is not enough; it requires everyone to work together to achieve it. More than fifty of you have come from various provinces, and upon returning, if you enthusiastically promote this in your respective provinces, rapid progress is certain. Mr. Wu Zhihui advocates for phonetic symbols. While phonetic symbols certainly have their imperfections, I, who studied them briefly one or two days in the past, have already forgotten them. However, for teaching illiterate people in rural areas, they are indeed easy to learn. Currently, there is no better method than phonetic symbols to enable the general public to become literate. When we earnestly promote this, within a few years, the number of literate people will certainly increase significantly. I remember when I was eleven or twelve years old, the elementary school taught me Romanization, and I went home and taught my mother and sisters-in-law, who all liked it very much. Learning phonetic symbols will certainly have the same effect. This is the most important point in promoting the popularization of education. I hope that when everyone promotes current Chinese education, what is most needed is not the expansion of higher education, but rather providing graduates of all levels of schools with a way out. Regardless of whether they are from universities, middle schools, or elementary schools, the majority of graduates are unemployed. This means that society adds a significant number of unemployed people each year. Without education, without a job, and unable to farm or work in industry, they can only turn to a path of decline, which is very dangerous. Taking military academies as an example, there are more than ten thousand graduates, but the military cannot accommodate them all. The academies have established advanced classes to provide placement, giving them opportunities for further study on one hand, and providing them with a way out on the other. Ordinary schools, of course, cannot operate in this way. Yesterday, I talked about promoting the popularization of agricultural education, which is a good way to remedy student unemployment. Students in universities, middle schools, and elementary schools should receive more agricultural training while they are in school, so that they can engage in agricultural work after graduation, without the risk of unemployment. And the national economy can also gradually become more prosperous. Secondly, regarding the rectification of the academic atmosphere, I said yesterday that if everyone earnestly takes responsibility to do it, it can certainly be done. Since I started running the military academy, I have trained tens of thousands of students over the past five years, and there has never been a case of strikes or disturbances. The students come from all over the country and are very diverse, with some being members of the Communist Party, some being nationalists, and some being anarchists. However, after only three months of training at the academy, they can be guided onto the right path, because young people have not been influenced by a bad environment, and their conscience is easily awakened. As long as the educators are sincere, it is impossible not to move young people. At present, academic thoughts and actions are very inconsistent. Those engaged in education, especially schools, and principals should take responsibility. Once the education policy is improved and decided, regardless of how society may oppose it, it must be carried out straightforwardly. We must absolutely not compromise with young students. Those in charge should not harbor selfish intentions, and should follow the rules and be punctual for classes. Students will not oppose them. If there is opposition, strict measures should be taken without any compromise. The gaze of the teachers can inspire respect in the students. Often, those who run schools dare not look students in the eye, and as a result, the students become more arrogant and the academic atmosphere deteriorates to an irreparable state. From today onwards, the education sector should take responsibility and work hard to implement the decided policy, regardless of any obstacles. In this way, education will certainly develop, and the path will certainly shine brightly. Please forgive me if what I have said is incorrect, he concluded. Next, Chung Yek-kwong, an expert in overseas Chinese education, delivered a response on behalf of the members, saying that over the past two days, Chairman Chiang had repeatedly emphasized important issues such as rectifying the academic atmosphere, promoting agricultural education, strictly implementing party education, and promoting phonetic symbols. Everyone is willing to sincerely absorb them, and the Chairman's instructions are more meaningful than the proposals discussed in the program. He expressed gratitude on behalf of everyone. Next, Chung continued to report on the current situation of overseas Chinese education, asking the government and education authorities to pay attention. The general idea was that if overseas Chinese education is not promoted further, the overseas Chinese will be assimilated by foreigners within twenty or thirty years in terms of knowledge. Those with insufficient knowledge will inevitably be oppressed by foreigners. Whether they die abroad or return to China, in short, in fifty years, there will be no overseas Chinese at all. Chairman Chiang listened to this with great attention. The meeting adjourned at about 7 PM.

Reading the Teacher Training Program (1) (Different) 153

The combined normal school system in the country was first established in Zhejiang, followed by Jiangsu. During the first National Education Conference, serious discussions arose on this issue. The education departments of Guangdong and Guangxi, National Sun Yat-sen University, the joint association of the normal science department of the Beijing Municipal Education Bureau and Central University, and experts Zhuang Zexuan and Cheng Bolu, among others, advocated that normal schools should be run independently. After several precise discussions, a remedial measure was finally achieved: "In order to promote compulsory education, independent normal schools should be established in each province in addition to the high school normal science department." The trend of opinion from all sides clearly favors the independence of normal schools. In fact, the combination and separation of middle school and normal school involve many time-sensitive and trivial issues. Education authorities who are concerned about this point raise objections. I believe that the education program is a fundamental plan for the next hundred years and cannot be sacrificed for the sake of temporary value. To refrain from eating for fear of choking is unacceptable.

Thoughts After Reading the Education Program Zhuang Zexuan 154

Although I had seen fragments of the program that is currently under discussion at the National Education Conference in various places, I did not read the entire thing until I arrived in Beijing the day before yesterday. The detailed plan is extensive, and of course, it is impossible to talk about it carelessly after reading it hastily in a short amount of time. However, as the Shen Bao has been urging me to write an article for several days, I will just talk about what I feel at the moment.

Regarding the various aspects of compulsory primary education for the masses, I have already responded to the solicitation of the Capital Central Daily and wrote an article entitled "On China's Compulsory Education Should Start at the Age of Ten" (see the first issue of the special publication of the National Education Conference in the newspaper on the 12th), in which I expressed some opinions. I will not talk about it for now.

Regarding the secondary education section, it was originally the most difficult to compile. Secondary education is the most difficult to run in ancient and modern times, both in China and abroad, because the content is the most complex. However, I often hear people say that the wealth and power of a country depend entirely on the quality of secondary-level talent. Therefore, I think that in the future, our country's education sector must pay special attention to this aspect. The current secondary education plan seems to still focus on academics and neglect vocational aspects. Originally, vocational education is very difficult to run in present-day China, but I believe that in the future, China's construction must make good use of vocational education as a tool for promotion. Both Ministers Chiang and Kong vaguely mentioned this idea when the conference opened, but they did not propose concrete measures. The program seems to pay little attention to this point as well. This may be because the conference must focus on a few major issues. I hope that if this conference does not have time to discuss this, the Ministry of Education can unite with the Construction Committee, the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, the Ministry of Railways, and the Ministry of Transportation, and add a number of industrial and educational experts to hold a joint meeting to discuss this issue specifically. In this way, not only will students have a way out and funding will have a source, but also the mind and material can be built up at the same time.

I believe that the reorganization of higher education is very important. I originally intended to join the higher education group and contribute some opinions, but after attending the meeting and seeing that a large number of people had already joined, I did not do so. I believe that high schools that focus on academics should be supervised by higher education institutions in various places, and people should be sent to participate in the high school graduation exams to improve and standardize the level of enrollment. It is best if each university, especially the national ones, can follow the American approach and set up a joint admissions committee. Those who pass the exam administered by this examination committee can enter any university and can transfer freely. Then each university can specialize in its strengths. Except for a few basic departments, they do not need to be established universally, but can focus on the development of a few departments. I believe that this is extremely important in today's China, where talents and funds are both difficult to obtain. Otherwise, although there are many universities, none of them has a strength. It is always these few people being pulled back and forth, which is the most painful thing for those who run universities. Of course, some departments need more, and three or four can be set up nationwide. Some can be set up with one or two nationwide. The funds saved can be used to increase equipment and increase salaries. In this way, academics can be improved and become independent. I hope that after this conference is over, the Ministry of Education can convene a university administrative conference to resolve this and other related issues.

Finally, regarding the issue of etiquette education, this program also seems to neglect this point somewhat. This may also be because the focus is on discussing a few issues. The results of this National Games were certainly very good. It is not easy to occupy a seat at the Far Eastern Games, let alone the fact that athlete sports are just a kind of stimulation, not a fundamental way to promote physical education. I believe that at least a middle school graduate should reach a certain physical education standard, and a university graduate should reach a higher standard (this is what we have already decided to implement at Sun Yat-sen University in Guangzhou). Special attention should be paid to the training of physical education teachers. These points all seem to be mentioned in the program.

The summary of my feelings is what our representative, Mr. Jin Xiangfan, said in his reply yesterday: This conference is to realize the Three Principles of the People's education determined by the last conference. Education on nationalism, people's livelihood, and people's rights should advance as a whole system. (April 16, in the capital)

Program Summary (3) 155

▲Plan to Improve and Develop Overseas Chinese Education

(1) Basis

1. The resolutions of the Overseas Chinese Education Conference assigned by the central government.

2. The Ministry of Education's plan to develop overseas Chinese education.

(2) Goals

1. To seek unique development.

2. To enhance national consciousness and the ability to self-govern and organize, and to cultivate the skills to improve life and develop production.

3. To seek reform and expansion of general education, vocational education, normal education, social education, and supplementary education.

(3) Organization

1. The Ministry of Education shall organize a design committee.

2. Before the Ministry of Education establishes a specialized department, administrative matters shall be handled by various departments. Overseas matters shall be managed by consuls. Each consulate shall have at least one commissioner, similar to a school inspector, who shall be selected and dispatched by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The number, qualifications, powers, and treatment of the commissioners commissioned by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs shall be determined by the two ministries. In areas where there is no consulate, personnel shall be dispatched by the Ministry of Education.

3. The people shall establish a General Overseas Chinese Education Association in Nanjing, with branches and overseas locations adopting a membership system. Commissioners shall be appointed from those who are familiar with overseas Chinese education, have experience, and are committed to overseas Chinese education to carry out, discuss, research, and promote various matters. The organizational regulations shall be promulgated by the government.

4. The local education association shall be established by the Party headquarters in conjunction with various social organizations to organize a education promotion committee, which shall hold education promotion activities at least twice a year.

(4) Funding

1. The central government shall allocate 500,000 yuan annually specifically for the development of overseas Chinese education.

2. To raise a fund of 10 million yuan, the National Government shall allocate 2 million yuan, Guangdong Province 600,000 yuan, Fujian Province 400,000 yuan, and 7 million yuan shall be raised through fundraising, with the interest to be used.

3. The funds for overseas locations shall be determined based on local conditions, by levying a business surtax, a property tax, a department store tax, or an annual, monthly, or special donation from shops or individuals. A funding committee shall be organized to handle this.

(5) Plan

1. The Ministry of Education's Design Committee shall draft plans for popularizing education, expanding junior high schools, expanding senior high schools, vocational schools, normal schools, promoting supplementary education, implementing social education, and reorganizing overseas Chinese education groups.

2. The Ministry of Education shall establish a committee to draft a plan to protect overseas Chinese education.

3. The Ministry of Education's Design Committee shall draft a plan to reorganize schools of all levels and types, as well as measures for the distribution and use of funds and interest from the fund allocated by the National Government for overseas Chinese education.

4. All plans should broadly solicit the opinions of consulate commissioners and overseas Chinese groups and cooperate with the education association.

5. Based on the actual situation, the design committee of the Ministry of Education and the opinions of overseas Chinese groups shall formulate all simple and easy-to-implement regulations and laws that do not conflict with public law.

(6) School Education

1. Establishment of Overseas Chinese Schools (1) Overseas Chinese-run schools shall be the principle and must be registered with the Ministry of Education. (2) Overseas Chinese may return to China to run secondary schools or above specifically for overseas Chinese children. (3) The Ministry of Education shall reward and subsidize overseas Chinese-run schools. (4) The Ministry of Education shall establish schools overseas as appropriate. (5) Overseas Chinese schools shall not receive subsidies from foreign governments or have foreigners as principals.

2. Organization of Overseas Chinese Schools (1) Overseas Chinese schools shall have a board of directors. The organizational regulations shall be determined by the Ministry, and various overseas locations shall choose one to implement. (2) The board of directors shall be responsible for raising funds, reviewing budgets and final accounts, protecting school property, hiring principals, and handling external affairs. The principal shall be responsible for managing school affairs, hiring teachers, and preparing budgets and final accounts. The principal may not terminate the contract halfway and may attend board of directors meetings. Individual opinions of the directors must be submitted to the board of directors for decision. (3) Overseas Chinese schools should have a faculty and staff council and may establish a student self-government association.

3. Funding for Overseas Chinese Schools (1) The funding standards shall be compiled by the education commissioner of the consulate and the education association. The ratio shall generally be the same as that of domestic primary and secondary schools. (2) The accounting law, school property management law, and economic transparency law shall generally be the same as those of domestic primary and secondary schools. (To be continued)
